<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_90ff0d59-288d-4358-8101-8079f6e47c59'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9118054921236062373">Are there other dimensions beyond those of our everyday experience? Are there gateways to parallel universes? What happened before the first day of Creation? These types of questions are at the center of current scientific activity. Indeed, many physicists today believe that there are other dimensions beyond the four of our space-time, and that a unified vision of the vari</span>
  <span id="freeText9118054921236062373" style="display:none">Are there other dimensions beyond those of our everyday experience? Are there gateways to parallel universes? What happened before the first day of Creation? These types of questions are at the center of current scientific activity. Indeed, many physicists today believe that there are other dimensions beyond the four of our space-time, and that a unified vision of the various forces of nature can be achieved, if we consider that everything we see around us, from the trees to the stars are nothing but vibrations in hyperspace. Hyperspace theory - and its more recent derivation, superstring theory - is the eye of this revolution. In this book, Michio Kaku shows us a fascinating panorama, which completely changes our view of the cosmos, and takes us on a dazzling journey through new dimensions: wormholes connecting parallel universes, time machines, "baby universes" and more. Similar wonders are emerging in some pages in which everything is explained with elegant simplicity and where the mathematical formulation is replaced by imaginative illustrations that allow the problems to be visualized. The result is a very entertaining and surprising book, which even leaves behind the greatest fantasies of the old science fiction authors.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9118054921236062373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

I r<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I've read both. Hyperspace is better written than Parallel Worlds, but Parallel Worlds has more current information on String Theory and M-Theory. I read Hyperspace first and then Parallel Worlds. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_5997987" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5997987" />
    <a title="Nathan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/368200-nathan"><img alt="Nathan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1202672364p2/368200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5997987?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan" href="/user/show/368200-nathan">Nathan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780195085143" href="/book/show/979636.Hyperspace">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Buck Rogers fans who build supercolliders.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/368200-nathan?shelf=science-physics-astronomy">science-physics-astronomy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/368200-nathan?shelf=science">science</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5997987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2214243567664316240">Michio Kaku apparently spent his childhood building super-colliders in his parents' garage. It paid off. He's clearly brilliant, and best of all, he's not lost his imagination. One sad fact of modern physicists is that precious few of them have any imagination, and are incapable of thought experiments and relative flights of fantasy. As Kaku has pointed out, fantasy fueled more great discoveries in science than pure science ever did on its own. In this book he uses what we know about quantum phy</span>
  <span id="freeText2214243567664316240" style="display:none">Michio Kaku apparently spent his childhood building super-colliders in his parents' garage. It paid off. He's clearly brilliant, and best of all, he's not lost his imagination. One sad fact of modern physicists is that precious few of them have any imagination, and are incapable of thought experiments and relative flights of fantasy. As Kaku has pointed out, fantasy fueled more great discoveries in science than pure science ever did on its own. In this book he uses what we know about quantum physics to explore possibilities formerly relegated exclusively to science fiction. In doing so, he should be admired. He is merely asking us to consider what some great minds in both literature and physics have imagined, and in doing so, manages to make what we do know seem almost simple by showing us how much we truly don't know. He's amazingly talented, imaginative, and best of all, he knows his math. He also knows how to use that math to dream of what's possible. An absolutely fun book to read.<br /><br />NC</span>
  <a data-text-id="2214243567664316240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who want to learn Quantum without having to put up with six years of math and science courses</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5418416" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9120743187694235572">This is the book that allowed me to fool an entire room of graduate students into thinking I was utterly Brilliant. It is a really good crash course on just what the hell Quantum, String, Unified Field Theory ad Superstring actually are. Lays down the history and concepts in a way that makes sense and makes you get it.<br/><br/>Particularly savvy readers will start making the other logical leaps. If we are thinking energy vibrating along a 10-dimensional string, what does that say about the frequency of s</span>
  <span id="freeText9120743187694235572" style="display:none">This is the book that allowed me to fool an entire room of graduate students into thinking I was utterly Brilliant. It is a really good crash course on just what the hell Quantum, String, Unified Field Theory ad Superstring actually are. Lays down the history and concepts in a way that makes sense and makes you get it.<br /><br />Particularly savvy readers will start making the other logical leaps. If we are thinking energy vibrating along a 10-dimensional string, what does that say about the frequency of sentience in the universe? Since energy can't go anywhere and sentience is a factor of energy, what the hell really does happen to us when we die?<br /><br />Enjoy your trip down the rabbit hole.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9120743187694235572" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1491786525" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Kelvin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45364364-kelvin"><img alt="Kelvin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454808848p2/45364364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1491786525?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelvin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelvin" href="/user/show/45364364-kelvin">Kelvin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45364364-kelvin?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45364364-kelvin?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45364364-kelvin?shelf=dnf-dislike">dnf-dislike</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45364364-kelvin?shelf=stem">stem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45364364-kelvin?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1491786525" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3190205809837445587">DNF at chapter 10. It was a bit too dry and technical for me. While the chapter names were intriguing and there were interesting anecdotes in each chapter, it was still slightly too boring, even with the pictures, for me to read into and understand the developments of modern physics. There wasn't much holding it together, i.e. the book only follows the overthrow of each theory as its organizing structure. It also seemed to ramble on with analogies that weren't that great to follow, eg the wood v</span>
  <span id="freeText3190205809837445587" style="display:none">DNF at chapter 10. It was a bit too dry and technical for me. While the chapter names were intriguing and there were interesting anecdotes in each chapter, it was still slightly too boring, even with the pictures, for me to read into and understand the developments of modern physics. There wasn't much holding it together, i.e. the book only follows the overthrow of each theory as its organizing structure. It also seemed to ramble on with analogies that weren't that great to follow, eg the wood vs marble and flatland comparisons. Though I'm sure that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/18800.Michio_Kaku" title="Michio Kaku" rel="nofollow noopener">Michio Kaku</a> is quite knowledgable about the theories mentioned in the book (as evidenced by his other books) I expected this book to be more in story form like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17033.Flatterland_Like_Flatland_Only_More_So" title="Flatterland Like Flatland Only More So by Ian Stewart" rel="nofollow noopener">Flatterland</a> and thus easier to read. Overall, this book was just disappointing for me. I expected it to be a fun and informative telling of the evolution of dimensional theories but ended up getting a book that was difficult to read and closer to a paper than novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3190205809837445587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_69169653" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69169653" />
    <a title="kesseljunkie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1846986-kesseljunkie"><img alt="kesseljunkie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483821046p2/1846986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69169653?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kesseljunkie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kesseljunkie" href="/user/show/1846986-kesseljunkie">kesseljunkie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385477055" href="/book/show/722419.Hyperspace">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69169653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14526455937462447573">It was OK just because the science fiction at the end was a lot of fun.<br/><br/>Dr. Kaku alternates through two styles -- talking to the reader like they're completely stupid and then talking to them like they've taken a college physics class. I'm neither, I understood what he was writing, and was just insulted. The cornerstone of Hyperspace theory is that there were 10 dimensions for a fraction of a fraction of time in the first fraction of time of existence for this universe, but 6 of them probably don</span>
  <span id="freeText14526455937462447573" style="display:none">It was OK just because the science fiction at the end was a lot of fun.<br /><br />Dr. Kaku alternates through two styles -- talking to the reader like they're completely stupid and then talking to them like they've taken a college physics class. I'm neither, I understood what he was writing, and was just insulted. The cornerstone of Hyperspace theory is that there were 10 dimensions for a fraction of a fraction of time in the first fraction of time of existence for this universe, but 6 of them probably don't exist since. Um, so there aren't 10 dimensions -- there might have been. And then the whole premise is that I should accept the premises in the book even though he acknowledges there may never be proof? <br /><br />And the difference between this and religion is....oh, I see, there is none. Fifth dimensional beings could exist, but not God? Interesting assertion. So long as we're just accepting things on faith, let me toss this one out there: God is a 5th dimensional being.<br /><br />But of course, it's sexy to act like you're smart -- and when someone like Dr. Kaku publishes a sexy bit of science fiction and calls it researched science, everyone's afraid to look like they don't "get it." It's like living in a Rand novel. <br /><br />It's OK to call bullsh*t on someone in the sciences, people. And in this instance, I do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14526455937462447573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3732627" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3732627" />
    <a title="Steve" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/227682-steve"><img alt="Steve" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3732627?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steve" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steve" href="/user/show/227682-steve">Steve</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385477055" href="/book/show/722419.Hyperspace">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">nerds like me</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3732627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11439299160252584858">If you've thought science is dull or perhaps too far beyond you, then please meet Michio Kaku. He writes about theoretical physics in a way that will fill you with wonder and possibility. He takes what would otherwise be very complex concepts and conveys them using metaphors that every average joe can understand. The number of a-ha moments I had reading this book were too many to count. What a terrific read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_7511845" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/7511845" />
    <a title="Shawna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/477898-shawna"><img alt="Shawna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1191988347p2/477898.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/7511845?book_show_action=true">Oct 09, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shawna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shawna" href="/user/show/477898-shawna">Shawna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer7511845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12829592952057646407">This is one of the popular science books that got me so interested in doing physics in the first place. Accessible to me before I even took a physics class, it should be accessible to most anyone with interest. Very interesting questions raised about space and time/parallel universes/etc. New ideas (as of date published: 1994) are discussed in a non-technical way. Also, very well written and easy to read (with humor and everything!).</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1904938935" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1904938935" />
    <a title="Rich Paz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7289539-rich-paz"><img alt="Rich Paz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475684437p2/7289539.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1904938935?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rich Paz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rich Paz" href="/user/show/7289539-rich-paz">Rich Paz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7289539-rich-paz?shelf=physics">physics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7289539-rich-paz?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7289539-rich-paz?shelf=inspirational">inspirational</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7289539-rich-paz?shelf=best-reads">best-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1904938935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3504353133220776561">I am now officially a Michio Kaku fan. This book explains physics as it should be taught in school. His simplistic approach begs the reader for more information. I also love physics now because I understand it a lot more thanks to Mr. Kaku's books. The school systems should think about this book as part of their cirriculum to teach the importance of understanding physics. Highly recommended.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385477055" href="/book/show/722419.Hyperspace">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18218857-marc?shelf=science">science</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18218857-marc?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18218857-marc?shelf=first-book-i-read-by-this-author">first-book-i-read-by-this-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18218857-marc?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1176064606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6534845602802065624">Michio Kaku makes some amazingly complex and mind-bending concepts accessible to the lay reader (i.e., me, and maybe you, too, if you're also not a physicist). He sprinkles the book with entertaining and informative anecdotes and his passion for the topic is infectious. Still, I shudder to think that no author ever addresses Schrödinger's ailurophobia. Here's hoping the 6-dimensional universe opens up just as this one closes!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2911666919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1062844131314232109">This is the first "hardcore" science book I've ever read, after wetting my appetite on <i>The Universe In Your Hands</i> and <i>Astrophysics For People In a Hurry</i>, and <b>needing</b> to dive deeper into these topics.<br/><br/>This book did not disappoint! <b>It's a bit dated,</b> as it was written in the 1990s, but I wanted to start with some of Kaku's earliest works to get a solid foundation of the concepts in here, before moving to his more recent books.<br/><br/><i>Hyperspace</i> has left my mind buzzing with possibilities, with the wonder of</span>
  <span id="freeText1062844131314232109" style="display:none">This is the first "hardcore" science book I've ever read, after wetting my appetite on <i>The Universe In Your Hands</i> and <i>Astrophysics For People In a Hurry</i>, and <b>needing</b> to dive deeper into these topics.<br /><br />This book did not disappoint! <b>It's a bit dated,</b> as it was written in the 1990s, but I wanted to start with some of Kaku's earliest works to get a solid foundation of the concepts in here, before moving to his more recent books.<br /><br /><i>Hyperspace</i> has left my mind buzzing with possibilities, with the wonder of the universe, as it took me through concepts like quantum physics, string theory, and higher dimensions.<br /><br />This has been rewarding as a theoretical physics fan, and inspiring as a science fiction writer.<br /><br />I'm excited to read Kaku's next book. It's already sitting on my shelf! 😌<br /><br />This was my first hardcore science book, but it definitely won't be the last. :)))</span>

In fact, according to this theory, matter is nothing but the harmonies created by this vibrating string. Since there are an infinite number of harmonies that can be composed for the violin, there are an infinite number of forms of matter that can be constructed out of vibrating strings. This explains the richness of the particles in nature. Likewise, the laws of physics can </span>
  <span id="freeText7202872117314404531" style="display:none">“According to string theory, if we could somehow magnify a point particle, we would actually see a small vibrating string. In fact, according to this theory, matter is nothing but the harmonies created by this vibrating string. Since there are an infinite number of harmonies that can be composed for the violin, there are an infinite number of forms of matter that can be constructed out of vibrating strings. This explains the richness of the particles in nature. Likewise, the laws of physics can be compared to the laws of harmony allowed on the string. The universe itself, composed of countless vibrating strings, would then be comparable to a symphony.”</span>

<div id="review_27426462" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/27426462" />
    <a title="Ricardo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1335294-ricardo"><img alt="Ricardo" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/27426462?book_show_action=true">Jul 16, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ricardo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ricardo" href="/user/show/1335294-ricardo">Ricardo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780385477055" href="/book/show/722419.Hyperspace">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer27426462" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer731561515084867295">It's up there, though not as accessible, as Hawking's "A Brief History of Time" and "The Universe in a Nutshell". Dr. Kaku does spend a considerable time walking the reader through how the theories of space-time and hyperspace arose and some of the historical and more mathematical stuff can be a little dense. However, the book opens really nicely with very vivid and amazing explanations of just how freaky hyperspace can be as well as the implications for the world of physics. The book also ends </span>
  <span id="freeText731561515084867295" style="display:none">It's up there, though not as accessible, as Hawking's "A Brief History of Time" and "The Universe in a Nutshell". Dr. Kaku does spend a considerable time walking the reader through how the theories of space-time and hyperspace arose and some of the historical and more mathematical stuff can be a little dense. However, the book opens really nicely with very vivid and amazing explanations of just how freaky hyperspace can be as well as the implications for the world of physics. The book also ends really well with how hyperspace can tell us something about how the universe will end as well as how it may help us, if we're still around, at that time as well as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17135.How_to_Build_a_Time_Machine" title="How to Build a Time Machine by P.C.W. Davies" rel="nofollow noopener">how to build a time machine</a> and the potential evolution of an intelligent species into one capable of manipulating time and space.<br /><br />I imagine his other book "Physics of The Impossible" which focuses more on trying to explain with physics for well-known sci-fi concepts would be as good as the beginning and end of this book. However, if you find that kind of topic, theoretical physics, black holes, time travel, 10 dimensional space, then I would recommend this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="731561515084867295" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2970802429" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2970802429" />
    <a title="Koen Crolla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3452722-koen-crolla"><img alt="Koen Crolla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501964713p2/3452722.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2970802429?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Koen Crolla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Koen Crolla" href="/user/show/3452722-koen-crolla">Koen Crolla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780198785033" href="/book/show/30413776-hyperspace">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3452722-koen-crolla?shelf=physics">physics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2970802429" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer984648580691316336">Hyper-generic pop-sci driven to its apex.<br/>For all that it pretends to be a coherent exploration of higher dimensions in both senses of the word (mathematical and sci-fi), <i>Hyperspace</i> is a series disconnected vignettes more concerned with hitting every topic on his list of popular science tropes than telling a coherent story—everything you could expect to be in a work of popular physics is in here, regardless of how much sense it makes to include it. If you're looking forward to seeing another tria</span>
  <span id="freeText984648580691316336" style="display:none">Hyper-generic pop-sci driven to its apex.<br />For all that it pretends to be a coherent exploration of higher dimensions in both senses of the word (mathematical and sci-fi), <i>Hyperspace</i> is a series disconnected vignettes more concerned with hitting every topic on his list of popular science tropes than telling a coherent story—everything you could expect to be in a work of popular physics is in here, regardless of how much sense it makes to include it. If you're looking forward to seeing another triangle drawn on a saddle or reading another synopsis of that Heinlein story about the girl who became her own parents, Kaku's your guy. (For a while he had me wondering if I'd already read this one and just forgot to review it, but no.)<br />The physics stuff is mostly⁰ covered in the exact same (shallow) way almost everyone else has covered it,¹ but he doesn't stick to that, because other writers don't. His inevitable discussion of things like the anthropic principle and the cosmological argument (you know: those things that were in all pop-sci from, say, the '80s all through <i>The God Delusion</i>, after which they mysteriously became less fashionable) seem calculated to miss the point in a way that's meant to annoy literally anyone with any opinion at all, but they're not even the most embarrassing sections of the book—that would be the ``futurology''² that takes up most of the last quarter of it (I hope you like reading about the Kardashev scale again!).<br /><br />In fairness I should also point out that this book was published in 1994, so it does predate a few hundred (but by no means all) of the books that made popular physics such a tired and derivative cottage industry; I don't think that excuses this one.<br />Writers who have written this exact book in a more competent way include Brian Greene, Brian Cox, and Michio Kaku.<br /><br />--------<br /><br />⁰ His discussion of Schrödinger's cat is notably worse.<br /><br />¹ Kaku did manage to do something Lee Smolin and Peter Woit never could: make me doubt that string theory is actually a meaningful thing and not just a mathematical artefact; a lot of the big insights in his own actual work that he brings up do seem to come down to realising something he came up with was just a way of rephrasing older laws.<br /><br />² A ``futurologist'', of course, being a sci-fi nerd with delusions of grandeur.</span>
  <a data-text-id="984648580691316336" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2305823138" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2305823138" />
    <a title="Cherie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3975787-cherie"><img alt="Cherie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557767180p2/3975787.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2305823138?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cherie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cherie" href="/user/show/3975787-cherie">Cherie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780195085143" href="/book/show/979636.Hyperspace">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2305823138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9113101521037316018">Michio Kaku uses great examples to help the reader understand the complex physics of parallel universes, time warps, the tenth dimension and more in <i>Hyperspace: A Scientific Odyssey Through Parallel Universes, Time Warps, and the Tenth Dimension</i>. Some of the pictures used to describe the physics made me laugh, particularly the one with Einstein staring at dinosaurs and the dinosaurs staring back.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2305823138">
  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_1595521514" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1595521514" />
    <a title="Benjamin Park" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44370756-benjamin-park"><img alt="Benjamin Park" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1497631041p2/44370756.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1595521514?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin Park" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin Park" href="/user/show/44370756-benjamin-park">Benjamin Park</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1595521514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8972731225290658980">Hyperspace makes the obtuse and opaque concepts of theoretical physics accessible to anyone with an interest in science. I was delighted to learn about the world of physics that lies beyond the three dimensions that we perceive. I did find parts of the book to be too dense or technical so I just skipped over those sections.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1216104124" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1216104124" />
    <a title="Jim Nielsen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24160488-jim-nielsen"><img alt="Jim Nielsen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379908918p2/24160488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1216104124?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim Nielsen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim Nielsen" href="/user/show/24160488-jim-nielsen">Jim Nielsen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1216104124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6673200163422577678">I found this to be an enjoyable, relatively accessible look at some of the most advanced theories of physics (and mathematics) in modern science. Granted, I didn't understand everything in this book, The overview on the brilliant theories of specific and general relativity and their consequences I found fascinating and understandable. Once you start getting into quantum theory and its mathematics things get a little strange and complicated. But why shouldn't they? Quantum mechanics, as the autho</span>
  <span id="freeText6673200163422577678" style="display:none">I found this to be an enjoyable, relatively accessible look at some of the most advanced theories of physics (and mathematics) in modern science. Granted, I didn't understand everything in this book, The overview on the brilliant theories of specific and general relativity and their consequences I found fascinating and understandable. Once you start getting into quantum theory and its mathematics things get a little strange and complicated. But why shouldn't they? Quantum mechanics, as the author explains, is a convoluted, ugly theory that is only still around because of its abilities to quite precisely predict experimental data. After an overview in these theories you begin to see the dichotomy between the two and how string theory represents a possibly elegant solution to unify all the laws of physics under a single theory. As the author states many times in the book, you begin to see how the laws of physics can be much more elegantly and beautifully expressed when brought into higher dimensions, an intriguing and fascinating concept. I couldn't put this book down!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6673200163422577678" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sZ3CB4RE1IMlZh8oFZED+NVkvmV8hCI7co48uHPD+tSjn6VmUZEqLpqnol7VwcRYgQ0yuZi8VrCtT8NnRIhSKw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('y82NPsZd0hWsVpkvsoaQLfk6SKj3G+7DsDTuvAE2V2XZz+pfE4gsuBOXJFly1leNrVPEdBMjmkhv9RFjNn3/mg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

That edition was on the cutting edge of what was then known about the origins and nature of the universe. But the intervening years have seen extraordinary advances in the technology of observing both the micro- and the macrocosmic worlds. These observations have confirmed many of Professor Hawking\'s theoretical predictions in the first edition of his book, including the recent discoveries of the Cosmic Background Explorer satellite (COBE), which probed back in time to within 300,000 years of the universe\'s beginning and revealed wrinkles in the fabric of space-time that he had projected. Everything. Yet, in recent years discoveries in physics and cosmology have led a number of scientists to conclude that our universe may be one among many. With crystal-clear prose and inspired use of analogy, Brian Greene shows how a range of different “multiverse” proposals emerges from theories developed to explain the most refined observations of both subatomic particles and the dark depths of space: a multiverse in which you have an infinite number of doppelgängers, each reading this sentence in a distant universe; a multiverse comprising a vast ocean of bubble universes, of which ours is but one; a multiverse that endlessly cycles through time, or one that might be hovering millimeters away yet remains invisible; another in which every possibility allowed by quantum physics is brought to life. Or, perhaps strangest of all, a multiverse made purely of math.\n\nGreene, one of our foremost physicists and science writers, takes us on a captivating exploration of these parallel worlds and reveals how much of reality’s true nature may be deeply hidden within them. And, with his unrivaled ability to make the most challenging of material accessible and entertaining, Greene tackles the core question: How can fundamental science progress if great swaths of reality lie beyond our reach?\n\nSparked by Greene’s trademark wit and precision, The Hidden Reality is at once a far-reaching survey of cutting-edge physics and a remarkable journey to the very edge of Feynman<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.25 avg rating &mdash; 15,878 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1985\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer2927467173800694430\">Famous the world over for the creative brilliance of his insights into the physical world, Nobel Prize-winning physicist Richard Feynman also possessed an extraordinary talent for explaining difficult concepts to the nonscientist. QED--the edited ver<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText2927467173800694430\" style=\"display:none\">Famous the world over for the creative brilliance of his insights into the physical world, Nobel Prize-winning physicist Richard Feynman also possessed an extraordinary talent for explaining difficult concepts to the nonscientist. QED--the edited version of four lectures on quantum electrodynamics that Feynman gave to the general public at UCLA as part of the Alix G. Mautner Memorial Lecture series--is perhaps the best example of his ability to communicate both the substance and the spirit of science to the layperson.\n\nThe focus, as the title suggests, is quantum electrodynamics (QED), the part of the quantum theory of fields that describes the interactions of the quanta of the electromagnetic field-light, X rays, gamma rays--with matter and those of charged particles with one another. By extending the formalism developed by Dirac in 1933, which related quantum and classical descriptions of the motion of particles, Feynman revolutionized the quantum mechanical understanding of the nature of particles and waves. And, by incorporating his own readily visualizable formulation of quantum mechanics, Feynman created a diagrammatic version of QED that made calculations much simpler and also provided visual insights into the mechanisms of quantum electrodynamic processes.\n\nIn this book, using everyday language, spatial concepts, visualizations, and his renowned &quot;Feynman diagrams&quot; instead of advanced mathematics, Feynman successfully provides a definitive introduction to QED for a lay readership without any distortion of the basic science. Characterized by Feynman\'s famously original clarity and humor, this popular book on QED has not been equaled since its publication.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"2927467173800694430\" href=\"#\" But today, de<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText16185504240994417527\" style=\"display:none\">In this groundbreaking book, the renowned theoretical physicist Lee Smolin argues that physics — the basis for all other sciences — has lost its way. For more than two centuries, our understanding of the laws of nature expanded rapidly. But today, despite our best efforts, we know nothing more about these laws than we knew in the 1970s. Why is physics suddenly in trouble? And what can we do about it?One of the major problems, according to Smolin, is string theory: an ambitious attempt to formulate a “theory of everything” that explains all the particles and forces of nature and how the universe came to be. With its exotic new particles and parallel universes, string theory has captured the public’s imagination and seduced many physicists.But as Smolin reveals, there’s a deep flaw in the theory: no part of it has been tested, and no one knows how to test it. In fact, the theory appears to come in an infinite number of versions, meaning that no experiment will ever be able to prove it false. As a scientific theory, it fails. And because it has soaked up the lion’s share of funding, attracted some of the best minds, and effectively penalized young physicists for pursuing other avenues, it is dragging the rest of physics down with it.With clarity, passion, and authority, Smolin charts the rise and fall of string theory and takes a fascinating look at what will replace it. A group of young theorists has begun to develop exciting ideas that, unlike string theory, are testable. Smolin not only tells us who and what to watch for in the coming years, he offers novel solutions for seeking out and nurturing the best new talent—giving us a chance, at long last, of finding the It is an exhilarating journey that begins with the Planck Epoch - the earliest period of time in the history of the universe - and goes through Einstein\'s Theory of Relativity, the Hubble Red Shift, and the detection of the Cosmic Microwave Background. These incredible discoveries all form the foundation for what we now understand as the &quot;standard model&quot; of the origin of the universe. The First Three Minutes examines not only what this model looks like, but also tells the exciting story of the bold thinkers who put it together.\n\nClearly and accessibly written, The First Three       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/18800.Michio_Kaku">About Michio Kaku</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3585787387403754618">(Arabic: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6155006._' rel='nofollow noopener'>ميشيو كاكو</a><br/>Russian: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4411713._' rel='nofollow noopener'> Митио Каку</a><br/>Chinese: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8282347' rel='nofollow noopener'>加來道雄</a><br/>Japanese: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14139696._' rel='nofollow noopener'>ミチオ・カク</a>)<br/><br/><br/>Dr. Michio Kaku is an American theoretical physicist at the City College of New York , best-selling author, a futurist, and a communicator and popularizer of science. He has written several books about physics and related topics of science.<br/><br/>He has written two New York Times Best Sellers, Physics of the Impossible (2008) and Physic</span>
  <span id="freeText3585787387403754618" style="display:none">(Arabic: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6155006._" rel="nofollow noopener">ميشيو كاكو</a><br />Russian: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4411713._" rel="nofollow noopener"> Митио Каку</a><br />Chinese: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8282347" rel="nofollow noopener">加來道雄</a><br />Japanese: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14139696._" rel="nofollow noopener">ミチオ・カク</a>)<br /><br /><br />Dr. Michio Kaku is an American theoretical physicist at the City College of New York , best-selling author, a futurist, and a communicator and popularizer of science. He has written several books about physics and related topics of science.<br /><br />He has written two New York Times Best Sellers, Physics of the Impossible (2008) and Physics of the Future (2011).<br /><br />Dr. Michio is the co-founder of string field theory (a branch of string theory), and continues Einstein’s search to unite the four fundamental forces of nature into one unified theory.<br /><br />Kaku was a Visitor and Member (1973 and 1990) at the Institute for Advanced Study in Princeton, and New York University. He currently holds the Henry Semat Chair and Professorship in theoretical physics at the City College of New York.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3585787387403754618" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
